NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Property – Alexandria Minerals Corp. 3

1.0 SUMMARY 
Geologica Groupe-Conseil Inc. ('Geologica') with the assistance of Mr. Eddy Canova, 

Vice-President of ALEXANDRIA MINERALS CORPORATION ('Alexandria') and Mr. Christian 
D'Amour, P. Geo., were asked to prepare a NI 43-101 Technical Evaluation Report on the Sleepy 
Property, located in the Abitibi Region of Quebec. 

Both Mr. Alain-Jean Beauregard of Geologica and Mr. Eddy Canova have visited the 
Sleepy property between September 10 and 16, 2007 and also throughout 2008 and 2009. 

The Sleepy property is located in the South-central portion of the Abitibi Greenstone Belt, 
which forms part of the Superior Structural Province. All the rocks of the area are Archean in age, 
except for NE-striking diabase dykes, which are Proterozoic in age. Volcanic rocks of the Malartic 
and Piché Groups predominate in the northern half of the area, while clastic sedimentary rocks of 
the Cadillac and Pontiac Groups are dominant in the southern half of the area. 

The most prominent structural feature of the area is the Cadillac Break (also known as the 
Cadillac Tectonic Zone ('CTZ')), which is located near, or at the contact between the Pontiac 
Group and the Malartic Group. It is a major tectonic zone that is characterized by intense shearing 
and mechanical deformation, and it can be traced from West to East over a total distance of 
approximately 210 kilometers from Kirkland Lake, Ontario in the west, to east of Louvicourt, 
Quebec. Later conjugate faulting and fracturing of both northeast and, to a lesser extent, 
northwest trends have also occurred along its length. 

Alexandria acquired the Sleepy property from Cambior Inc. (later IAMGOLD Corp.), part of 
four, which consist of the Akasaba, "Bloc Sud" West, "Bloc Sud" Sleepy and the "Bloc Sud" Trivio 
properties. These properties are located along the Cadillac Break or along the northern contact of 
the eastward continuation of the Cadillac Break. 

The Cadillac Break is one of the most important metallogenic features in the Val-d'Or area. 
Several past producers (e.g. East Malartic, Barnat-Sladen, and O'Brien) and recent discoveries 
such as the Lapa and the Goldex Mines of Agnico-Eagle Mines Inc. are spatially associated with 
the Cadillac Break and /or related subsidiary structures. 

 In November 2009, LTM Laboratory of Val-d'Or has completed various recovery 
and metallurgical tests on seven (7) samples: one sample of 1 kg and three samples of 3 
kg, which were collected on mineralized core from DDH IAX-09-49. The samples were 
crushed at various grain sizes (400, 200, 65, 35 and 10 mesh), passed through a Knelson 
concentrator, then cyanidated and flocculated. 

 It was concluded that: the ore is easy to grind; the gold is easily recoverable by 
cyanidation; the cyanide consumption is low; gravimetric recovery with a Knelson 
concentrator does not necessarily improve recovery when the ore is concentrated prior to 
cyanidation; the best flocculent for the Sleepy property ore is Percol 338. 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Property – Alexandria Minerals Corp. 4

It would be advisable to continue the testing with other grinding size and cyanide 
exposition time to analyse the grinding-cyanide curves. Moreover, very fine grinding and 
concentration with a Knelson concentrator followed with longer cyanide solution 
exposition is recommended. The LTM Laboratory report is presented in Appendix VII. 

Recently, M. Christian D'Amours from Geopointcom (Val-d'Or, Quebec) was 
commissioned by Alexandria to complete a mineral resource estimate. In using a minimal 
horizontal thickness of 3 meters and a cut off grade of 2.00 g/t Au; the inferred resources of the 
Sleepy zone are estimated at 1,557,000 tonnes at 3.00 g/t Au for a total of 150,400 ounces of 
gold.

The properties of Alexandria Minerals Corp. are all strategically well located with respect 
to the Cadillac Break and its conjugate auriferous structures (Sigma II) in the Val-d'Or Camp. 
Several base metals and gold mines and deposits such as Sigma, Lamaque, Bevcon, Orenada, 
Dorval, Akasaba, Monique and others are located along the eastern part of this tectonic zone and 
are contiguous to or on the properties of Alexandria. The presence of these deposits in the 
immediate vicinity of the land holdings confirms the potential for finding either new mineralized 
zone and/or extensions of existing ones. 

 Although low gold values have been found locally on some of the Cadillac Fault Group of 
properties, past exploration efforts have led to the discovery of several significant mineralized 
zones and occurrences. Moreover, the average depth investigated by diamond drilling on the 
properties in the past is approximately 150 meters. The depth extensions of northeast trending 
splay structures from the Cadillac Break and Z shaped folds defined at shallow elevations have 
historically proven to be favorable exploration targets. Recent discoveries at depth attest to the 
potential of the region: Agnico Eagle's Lapa and Goldex deposits on or near the Cadillac Break 
has stimulated new exploration interest in the region, particularly at depths greater than 500 
meters.

 Due to the presence of numerous interesting occurrences, geological structures, 
geophysical, and geochemical targets on the Sleepy property, the authors recommend a 
complementary exploration program totaling $1,256,000.



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

Technical Drill Report on the Sleepy property – Alexandria Minerals Corp. 5

2.0 INTRODUCTION 

Geologica Groupe-Conseil Inc. ('Geologica') with the assistance of Mr. Eddy Canova, 
Vice-President of ALEXANDRIA MINERALS CORPORATION ('Alexandria') and Mr. Christian 
D'Amours, P. Geo., were asked to prepare a NI 43-101 Technical Evaluation Report on the 
Sleepy Property, located in the Abitibi Region of Quebec (Figure 1). 

All the assessment work records (statutory work) registered with the Quebec Department 
of Natural Resources (MRNFQ) were carefully examined. The reports and the geological maps 
published by the MRNFQ, recent work, and works currently in progress were also reviewed. This 
report contains an exhaustive evaluation of all available data, as well as recommendations for 
follow-up works designed to access and increase the auriferous potential of the properties. 

The Sleepy property (Figure 2) is located in the south-central portion of the Abitibi Greenstone 
Belt, which produced more than 170 million ounces over the last 90 years, and forms part of the 
Superior Structural Province. The regional geology of the area is presented on the Figure 3.

2.4 Qualifications and Field Involvement of Consultant 

Geologica Inc. independence is ensured by the fact that it holds no equity in any project 
and that its ownership rests solely with its staff. This allows Geologica to provide its clients with 
conflict-free and objective recommendations on crucial judgment issues.  

Neither Geologica nor any of its employees in the preparation of this report has any 
beneficial interest in Alexandria. Geologica will be paid a fee for this work in accordance with 
normal professional consulting practice. 

The following Geologica staff, Jean-Alain Beauregard and Daniel Gaudreault acting as 
Qualified Persons under National Instrument 43-101, conducted personal inspections of the 
Cadillac Break properties during the period between August 2007 and October 2007. 

Statements of qualification for these persons are included in Section 9.0 (Item 24). 

The authors from Geologica Inc. have reviewed and analysed data provided by Iamgold, 
Alexandria Minerals Corp., their consultants and previous owners of the property, and have drawn 
their own conclusions there from, augmented by its direct field examination. Geologica has not 
carried out any independent exploration work, drilled any holes core samples on the Sleepy 
property. However, the presence of gold in the local rocks is substantiated by the drilled core by 
Iamgold and other owners and the numerous prospectors in the area.  Geologica has not 
performed any resource estimations on the property. During the field visit some local surface or 
grab samples and accompanying photos were taken by one of the authors (A.J. Beauregard) in 
order to confirm when available the presence of mineralizations. 

While exercising all reasonable due-diligence in checking, confirming and testing the data, 
Geologica has relied upon the data presented by Alexandria in formulating its opinion.

4.0 PROPERTY DESCRIPTION AND LOCATION 

In 2007, Alexandria Minerals purchased the mineral rights of four properties from Cambior 
Inc. (later IAMGOLD Corporation) for three equal, annual payments totaling $500,000 in cash or 
shares. These are: Akasaba, "Bloc Sud" West, "Bloc Sud" Trivio, and "Bloc Sud" Sleepy. 
Alexandria has completed the first of the three annual payments. The group comprises eighty 
nine (89) claims and one (1) mining concession, the historic Akasaba Mine (Figure 2). The 
properties covered 2,291.25 hectares. All the claims are 100% Alexandria interest except for the 
CM 467 Mining Concession, which is still Iamgold 100% responsible. 

The "Bloc Sud" Sleepy (named "Sleepy") property is located about 30 kilometers to the 
ESE of Val-d'Or, Abitibi in range V of Louvicourt Township, NTS 32C/03 at approximately 
77°24'W and 48'03'2''N. The Sleepy property comprises eight (8) contiguous claims (312.4 
hectares) (Figure 2), and hosts the Sleepy Deposit, which contains 1,557,000 tonnes grading 3.00 
g/t of gold (Au). 

 The property is free and clear of any and all liens, charges, encumbrances, claims (actual, 
pending or threatened), royalties or interests of others of whatsoever nature and kind 
("Encumbrances").  



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

Technical Drill Report on the Sleepy property – Alexandria Minerals Corp. 8

5.0 ACCESSIBILITY AND PHYSIOGRAPHY 

Topography and Vegetation

 The area is characterized by a low relief and is mainly covered by boreal forest, reforested 
areas and wetlands (50%). The overburden thickness ranges from 10 to 30 meters, with an 
average of 20 meters on the property (Overburden Drilling Management report, 1988, Geospex, 
1998).

Access

 The property can be reached by highway 117 and several forest roads. Range IV-V line 
can be used by foot or on the Louvicourt River by boat. Several tertiary roads were made in 1988 
for the Inverse Circulation Drill program conducted across the property.  

Climate and Infrastructure

The local climate is that of the Canadian Shield at this latitude, that is to say 
typically continental, with hard winters extending from October to April, and with snow 
accumulations that can reach several meters and precipitation of 80 centimeters per year. 
The summers are relatively hot and fairly wet.

7.0 GEOLOGICAL SETTING 

7.1 Regional Geology 

All the rocks of the area are Archean in age, except for the north east striking diabase 
dykes which are Proterozoic in age. Volcanic rocks predominate in the northern half of the area 
while clastic sedimentary rocks are dominant to the south. 

The volcanic rocks of the Val-d'Or-Malartic area are subdivided into two principal groups, 
the Lower Malartic Group (containing the La Motte-Vassan, Jacola and Dubuisson Formations) is 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

Technical Drill Report on the Sleepy property – Alexandria Minerals Corp. 10

located in the northern portion of the region, and the Upper Malartic Group (containing the Héva 
and Val-d'Or Formations) is located in the southern portion of the region.  Slivers of the Piché 
Group also occur as entrainments along the Cadillac Break. The Lower Malartic Group volcanic 
rocks are dominated by submarine komatiites and tholeiitic basaltic flows. The Upper Malartic 
Group volcanic rocks range from tholeiitic to calc-alkaline in affinity (Imreh, 1984), and include 
flows of mafic to intermediate composition, rhyolitic flows, flow breccias, and pyroclastic rocks of 
felsic to intermediate composition. 

Clastic sedimentary rocks of the aerially extensive Pontiac Group overlie the Malartic 
Group volcanic rocks in the southern part of the region. These sedimentary rocks are composed 
of turbidite sequences consisting of interbedded greywacke, siltstone, argillite and conglomerate. 
Similar clastic sedimentary rocks of the Cadillac and Kewagama Groups occur further to the west 
in the Malartic area, or are also entrained within the Cadillac Break in the Val-d'Or area. 

Several large granitoid intrusions have been emplaced into the local stratigraphy. The 
largest of these are the post-kinematic Lacorne and Pascalis Batholiths. The Bourlamaque 
Batholith (Figure 3) is a synvolcanic granitoid intrusion described as a quartz diorite by Campiglio 
(1977). The Centre Post Intrusion (also known as the East Sullivan Pluton) is a stock of 
intermediate composition that exhibits a zonation from a monzonitic core to a dioritic rim.  It has 
been emplaced into the Upper Malartic Group rocks. Numerous other smaller intrusions, including 
gabbro-diorite sills of possible sub-volcanic origin and younger feldspar porphyry dykes, occur 
throughout the region. 

The Upper and Lower Malartic Group rocks have an overall east-west strike and dip 
steeply to the north. The sequence becomes younger in age to the south and forms the south 
limb of the LaMotte-Vassan regional anticlinorium. Recent geological work in the Malartic area, 
where interference fold patterns are observed, demonstrates that at least two phases of ductile 
deformation have affected the Val-d'Or-Malartic area supracrustal rocks. The first episode 
involved folding about north-south oriented fold axes. The second episode re-folded the sequence 
about east-west trending fold axes and was the dominant folding event. 

The most prominent structural feature of the area is the Cadillac Break also known as the 
Cadillac Tectonic Zone (CTZ), which is situated at or near the contact between the Pontiac and 
the Malartic Groups. It is a major tectonic zone characterized by intense shearing and mechanical 
deformation that can be traced from West to East over a total distance of approximately 210 
kilometers from Kirkland Lake to Louvicourt.  Later subsidiary and conjugate faulting and 
fracturing along both north-east and, to a lesser extent, north-west trends have also occurred 
along its axis. 

The metamorphic grade of the Malartic Group volcanic stratigraphy is middle green schist 
facies, as indicated by a chlorite-epidote-carbonate mineral assemblage in rocks of mafic 
composition. The regional metamorphic grade increases towards the south to upper greenschist 
facies in the vicinity of the Cadillac Break, and to amphibolite facies further south. 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                11

7.2 Local Geology 

 Rocks of the Upper Malartic Group underlie the Sleepy property. These consist of 
intermediate agglomerates and tuffs with intercalated dacitic units (lava and agglomerate), 
and an andesitic unit and a thick intermediate spherulitic package of flows overlie the latter to 
the south. They are cut by dioritic to gabbroic sills, which intrude them in an ESE-WNW 
direction. One of these sills, the Vicour Sill hosts the Sleepy Zone and the Sigma II deposit. It 
is a differentiated intrusion of dioritic to gabbroic composition, varying from 100 to 350 meters 
in width. 

There are a number of synvolcanic and syntectonic dykes in the area of the 
properties that are of felsic to mafic composition.  On the Sleepy property a number of 
gabbroic to quartz-diorite dykes-sills are observed intruding the intermediate to mafic 
volcanics of the area.  The tonalites – quartz-diorites and gabbros are differentiated, 
magnetic and demonstrate alterations that consist of epidotization, silicification with some 
leucoxene (after magnetite).  The Vicour sill is a 100 m to 350 m wide differentiated gabbroic 
dyke that trends 110º dipping steeply to the south.  Sections that are altered in the Vicour sill 
are generally the sections that are mineralized.  The geological environment is similar to the 
Sigma-2 mine (Figure 5). 

The units on the property trend east-northeast with steep dips to the south with the 
tops being to the south.  Shears parallel to the Cadillac Fault along an east-southeast trend 
and subsidiary shears trending northeast and displacing the gabbroic dykes-sills dextrally.  
The northeast trending structures are important in some of the mineralized systems i.e., 
Sleepy Zone.

Mineralization occurs in the Vicour sill, which is differentiated, varying from a fine 
grain gabbro to coarse and granophyric, crystalline, magnetic gabbro. Fabrics typical of 
magmatic origin include magmatic flow and depositional characteristics, intergrown sulfide 
grains and the possibility of net texture typically in a layered complex.  Mineralization in the 
Vicour Sill is along sections of the gabbros that are highly altered with albite (albitization), 
quartz, chlorite (alteration of amphiboles), as demonstrated by a petrographic study.  These 
sections will have 2% to 6% disseminated pyrite and massive pyrite near the quartz veins.  
The Sleepy zone occurs along such a zone and a resource of 152,471 tonnes grading 5.1 g/t 
was identified in 1988 and 1998 (Houle 1988; Chenard et Lacey 1998), an historic resource 
which is pre National Instrument 43-101 and therefore non-compliant. The Sleepy Zone 
occurs in a similar geological context as the Sigma-2 mine that produced 1.8 million tonnes 
with a grade of 2.7 g/t Au, producing 152,255 oz Au.  Along the same mineralizing horizons 
(quartz-diorites – tonalites), but 1.2 km to the east of the Sleepy Zone a drill hole BS-05-32 
intersected mineralization grading 18.1 g/t Au over 1.5 m (Figure 5).  

8.0 DEPOSIT TYPES 

 The Sleepy property hosts the historic Sleepy deposit (152,471 t @ 5.1 g/t Au, Houle, 
1988, Chénard and Lacey, 1998, Grondin and Brisson, 2006). The geology of this deposit is 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                12

the same as the Sigma-II Mine located 4.5 km west along strike. The Sigma II mine, 
however, the contains arsenopyrite, a mineral lacking at Sleepy. The host for these deposits 
is the Vicour Sill, a differentiated gabbro-tonalite sill, with a distinctive blue quartz tonalite 
facies. This facies contains 2 to 4 % pyrite as disseminated grains and as veinlets. The sill is 
primarily granophyric, highly magnetic gabbro, and highly altered sections which are rich in 
albite, quartz, and chlorite (Renou 2008) are similar to tonalite compositionally.  The altered 
zone tends to be located approximately 100 m north of the southern contact of the Vicour 
Sill.

9.0 MINERALIZATION 

 In the differentiated Vicour Sill, the Sleepy Zone mineralization is hosted within an 
intensely albitized alteration zone with blue quartz eyes (possibly of tonalitic composition 
(Renou 2008)), and with 2% to 10% pyrite content and minor chalcopyrite. The pyrite is 
disseminated, in irregular stringers, and in small quartz veinlets (1 to 5 centimeters), locally 
with visible gold, (Houle, 1988). Widths of the mineralized zone vary from 2 to 22.6 meters 
(true width). The zone is 450 meters long and a maximum depth of 360 meters, and is open 
on all sides. 

 Other exploration work reports diamond drill values up to 2.01 % Cu  over 0.15 meter 
and 4.35 g/t Au over 0.18 meter in hole TL-13 (GM 01538), associated with quartz veins 
within the Vicour Sill and intermediate altered rocks (SOQUEM's Plans). Alteration and 
sulphides (pyrite) within sheared intermediate volcanic rocks were also observed by the 
writers during the diamond drill hole core sampling and verification procedure. 

 About 1 km east of the Sleepy Zone, hole BS-05-32 intersected 18.1 g/t Au over 1.5 
meters, and hole BS-05-33 intersected 9.5 g/t Au over 1.5 meters and 7.5 g/t Au over 1.5 
meters, the two intervals separated by 6.5 meters. Both holes were located at a similar 
stratigraphic position as the Sleepy Zone, within the Vicour Sill (Grondin and Brisson, 2006). 

 Similar gold mineralization can be found in the Vicour Sill at the Sigma II deposit 
(reserves of 1,2Mt @ 2.8 g/t Au), located 3 kilometers west of the property where gold 
mineralization is also associated with the more felsic facies of that sill: quartz stockwork 
veins within tonalite-granodiorite. The gold bearing veins are mostly sub-horizontal (Sauvé et 
al, 1993). 

 Gold, copper and zinc showings occur about 500 meters north of the Sleepy Block 
boundary in intermediate to felsic volcanic rocks of the Malartic Group with values up to 9.9 
g/t Au over 0.4 meter; 3% Cu over 3.6 meters and 17% Zn over 3.7 meters in diamond drill 
holes (MRNFQ Files # GM 22230, 24423 and 44853). Very little exploration work has been 
done to explore the volcanic rocks south of the Vicour sill. 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                13

10.0 EXPLORATION 

Compilation, Reports

 In 2007 Abitibi Geophysics re-interpreted a regional Fugro Mega TM survey originally 
completed in the late 1990's, covering the entire Cadillac Break property. Abitibi Geophysics 
also stitched, compiled, and re-interpreted, Induced Polarization (IP) data collected over 
many of the claim groups that comprise the Cadillac Break Properties. Approximately 350 
line-kilometers were evaluated, and have presented the data in plan view and on pseudo-
sections.  

 Technologie Earthmetrix Inc. completed a combined structural and lithogeochemical 
study, using airphoto and satellite imagery together with geochemical trends and anomalies 
for Au and Cu in soils and rocks, in 2007. 

 Alexandria Minerals Corporation completed the compilation of historical drill logs  
entering all the data into a mining software program (Gems) which will help identify 
preferable geological units, alteration and mineralization patterns. 

Field Work

During the period of September 2006 to April 2007 Alexandria Minerals Corporation 
(in a JV with Cambior) carried out an IP survey and drilled two holes on the Sleepy zone.  
During the period of December 2006 and February 2008, a re-interpretation of the airborne 
geophysics and Induced polarization (IP) ground surveys was carried out on all the 
properties.

On the Bloc Sud Sleepy property between the periods of September 2006 and April 
2007 Cambior (in JV with Alexandria Minerals Corporation) carried out an IP survey with 
lines spaced at 100 m. Property wide geophysical re-interpretations of a Fugro Mega TM 
survey done in the late 1990's, carried out by Abitibi Geophysics, re-interpreting the EM and 
the magnetics. Alexandria Minerals Corporation also commissioned Abitibi Geophysics to 
reinterpreted all the IP Resistivity surveys done on the properties, for a total of 330 line 
kilometers of IP, with preparation of new pseudo-sections. All of this geophysics was carried 
out between December 2006 and February 2008. 

A structural geological study of the Val-d'Or Camp was carried out between the 
periods of December 2006 and March 2007.  This structural study was assisted by the use of 
airphoto and satellite imagery interpretation, and litho geochemical trends (Au and Cu) which 
has helped define drill targets.  Fifty drill targets (50) have been outlined through out the 
Cadillac Break properties, and fifteen (15) are outlined on the eastern properties (on 7 
properties). 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                14

11.0 DRILLING 

 In 2007, Alexandria drilled two holes totaling 580.6 meters, IAX-07-14 and IAX-07-15
(Table 2), on the Sleepy Zone in order to test the extension of mineralization at the historic 
deposit. Both holes had thick overburden with depths of 69 meters to 73 meters. The holes 
began in intermediate to mafic flows with little or no mineralization. These volcanic units are 
followed by coarse grained, granophyric, chloritized, magnetic gabbro and diorite up to 150 
meters thick, with weak epidote alteration occasionally cut by quartz veins locally containing 
pyrite and chalcopyrite. More siliceous varieties or altered zones appear as quartz-diorite and 
tonalite, and host blue quartz (10% to 25%) and 2% to 10% disseminated pyrite.  

In 2007 Alexandria Minerals Corporation followed up with a drilling program of the 
Sleepy Zone drilling two holes totalling 580.6 m. The two holes IAX-07-14 and 15 (Fig 5), 
tested extensions of the gold mineralization in the Vicour Sill. The holes intersected basalts, 
andesites, and dacites followed by a thick granophyric to fine grained massive  gabbro. The 
granophyric gabbro is magnetic, with abundant blue quartz-eyes, carbonate and chlorite 
alteration, and is locally sheared. The altered section of the gabbro, identified as the Sleepy 
Zone is albitized, silicified, and chloritized, is penetrated by fine quartz veinlets and contains 
2% to 10% pyrite and minor chalcopyrite. This altered zone contains up to 70% albite (Renou 
2008), with blue quartz eyes, 5% chlorite and 2% to 10% disseminated pyrite. Quartz content 
varies between 10% to 25%, with 2% to 5% narrow quartz veining.  

Drill hole IAX-07-14 intersected mineralization grading 2.39 g/t Au over 16.0 m 
(including 3.35 g/t Au over 10.8 m) at the interval 203.9 m (Table 3). Drill hole IAX-07-15 
tested the eastern extension, and did not return anomalous values in the pyritic altered 
sections. 

In 2008 Alexandria Minerals Corp. continued the drilling program on the Sleepy 
property by drilling holes IAX-08-28, 29, 30, 31, 34, 35, 36, 37, 39 and 40, for a total of 
4,431.1 m.  The five drill holes IAX-08-28, 29, 30, 31 and 34 were drilled on the east side of 
Sleepy Lake testing the Sleepy Zone mineralization (Figure 5, Tables 2 and 3). The five drill 
holes IAX-08-35, 36, 37, 39 and 40 were drilled on the west side of Sleepy Lake, testing the 
western extension of the Sleepy Zone mineralization in the Vicour Sill (Figure 5, Table 2 and 
3), and also testing gold mineralization in altered volcanic environments.   

Drill hole IAX-08-28 had three mineralized sections occurring at 30.4 m grading 1.64 
g/t Au over 0.70 m in basalt with 1% pyrite, at 265.3 m grading 1.09 g/t Au over 1.00 m in a 
faulted basalt with 1% pyrite, and at 309.0 m grading 0.62 g/t Au over 1.20 m in quartz- 
bearing gabbros that resembles the mineralized zone (Figure 5 and Table 3). The second 
hole, IAX-08-29, drilled on Sleepy Lake intersected mineralization at 134.65 m grading 1.03 
g/t Au over 12.95 m (including 1.30 g/t Au over 8.95 m and 2.71 g/t Au over 3.20 m) in 
altered gabbro, with blue quartz, 3% to 7% pyrite, and 1% pyrrhotite. The third hole, IAX-08-
30, drilled below drill hole IAX-08-29, intersected mineralization at 84.70 m, grading 4.90 g/t 
Au over 0.80 m in magnetic altered basalts with 2% pyrite and chalcopyrite. IAX-08-30 also 
intersected mineralization at 346.85 m grading 2.42 g/t Au over 11.30 m in altered gabbros 
(albitized, silicified and chloritized) with 3% to 7% pyrite (Sleepy Zone). These results confirm 
the extension of the mineralization 100 m to 150 m west of, and 120 m to 150 m deeper than,  
previously known mineralization, giving the zone an east-west dimension of 400 m plus and 
vertically 250 m plus. The mineralization is open westward, which warrants two to three 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                15

sections of drilling with approximately 9 drill holes. A program in 2009 has been designed 
calling for a total 2330 m in five drill holes of drilling to test the westward extension of the 
mineralization and at depth testing new zones. The drilling has to be done in the winter on 
the ice.

Drill hole IAX-08-31 was completed 500 m east of IAX-07-14, on the eastern side of 
the Sleepy Zone, and drill hole IAX-08-34 was completed 1300 m east, to test the eastern 
extensions of gold mineralization in the Vicour gabbro sill.  Drilling was also carried out to the 
west of the Lake Sleepy testing western extensions of the mineralization with the holes IAX-
08-35, IAX-08-36 and IAX-08-37. The gabbro sill was encountered with silicified sections and 
mineralized with pyrite. 

Drill hole IAX-08-31 is 640 m east of IAX-08-29 (Fig 5), testing the eastern extension 
of the Sleepy mineralization. The drill hole did not intersect mineralization and it appears the 
hole was below the mineralized trend.   

Drill hole IAX-08-34 was 1490 m east of drill hole IAX-08-29 testing gold 
mineralization extensions from drill hole BS-05-33, with grades of 9.5 g/t Au over 1.50 m and 
7.1 g/t Au over 1.50 m, and extensions from the hole BS-05-32, with grades of 18.1 g/t Au 
over 1.50 m (Fig 5 and Table 2, 3). The drill hole did not have any anomalous gold values but 
had an intersection at 45.50 m grading 0.34 % Cu and 4.96 g/t Ag over 35.70 m occurring in 
medium grained altered andesites – dacites with chlorite alteration, 3% to 4% pyrite and 1% 
disseminated and veinlet chalcopyrite. This may indicate a favorable volcanic environment 
for sulphide mineralization and a ground Deep EM survey was carried out on 8 lines to verify 
the extent of the mineralization. Near the drill hole IAX-08-34 at least two holes are 
warranted with Deep EM results (approximately 600 m). The compilation of the Sleepy zone 
sections and mineralized zone are presented on the longitudinal with the recent 2007 and 
2008 drilling results being presented (Fig 5).    

The exploration drill holes IAX-08-35, IAX-08-36 and IAX-08-37 (Fig 3 and 5, and 
table 2, 3) are located on the west side of Sleepy Lake and of the Sleepy zone.  A number of 
anomalous copper intersections occur within the Vicour Gabbro sill (Fig 5 and Table 3).  Drill 
hole IAX-08-35 intersected 0.15% Cu over 2.60 m at 318.4 m in gabbro with 2% to 5% pyrite 
and trace to 2% chalcopyrite. At 374.2 m the drill core intersected 0.06% Cu over 1.50 m in a 
gabbro with 3% to 4% pyrite-chalcopyrite. At 467.8 m the drill core intersected 0.11% Cu 
over 9.20 m in gabbro with 1% to 3% pyrite and chalcopyrite. Drill hole IAX-08-36 did not 
intersect any anomalous gold values but did intersect 0.10% Cu over 0.9 m at 356.7 m, 
0.95% Cu over 0.3 m at 361.2 m, 0.21% Cu over 2.25 m at 371.2 m, and 0.12% Cu over 2.1 
m at 395.5 m. These intersections occur in the gabbro sill that is medium to coarse grain, 
magnetic, with 3% to 4% carbonate veins and 1% to 2% pyrite – chalcopyrite.  Drill hole IAX-
08-37 is 750 m west of the drill hole IAX-08-36 and it also intersected anomalous copper 
results: 0.06% Cu over 3.60 m at 168.0 m, occurring in deformed basalts with 1% to 2% 
pyrite-chalcopyrite just south of the gabbro sill.  A second intersection occurs at 205.0 m and 
grades 0.06% Cu over 1.30 m in mylonitized diorites – leucogabbros with 10% to 15% pyrite 
and pyrrhotite, and traces of chalcopyrite.  These highly anomalous Cu values observed in 
holes IAX-08-35, IAX-08-36 and IAX-08-37 occur in this differentiated gabbro Vicour sill.  In 
the drill core it is observed that the gabbro varies from fine-medium grained massive phases 
to coarser prismatic, granophyric magnetic phases.   

Drill hole IAX-08-39, located west of Sleepy Lake (Figure 5 and table 2, 3) and just 
south of the hole IAX-08-36, tested the copper mineralization in dacites just south of the 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                16

gabbroic sill (similar to drill hole IAX-08-34 which had intersected 0.34% Cu over 35.7 m).  
The hole penetrated a series of intermediate volcanics (dacites and andesites) that are 
chloritized and mineralized with pyrite and chalcopyrite. These are followed to the south by 
intermediate to felsic tuffs and lapilli tuffs that are also chloritized, carbonatized and silicified, 
with 1% to 2% pyrite and chalcopyrite. Drill hole IAX-08-39 had a number of intersections at 
65.85 m grading 0.11% Cu and 0.03 g/t Au over 1.05 m, at 89.10 m grading 0.12% Cu and 
0.01 g/t Au over 2.45 m, at 121.40 m grading 0.11% Cu and 0.05 g/t Au over 1.50 m, at 
146.80 m grading 0.17% Cu over 1.50 m and at 185.80 m grading 0.29% Cu over 6.50 m.  
These are all south of the gabbro sill and it identifies an area of dacites and intermediate tuffs 
that are mineralized in copper. The following hole to the west IAX-08-40 also encountered 
intermediate volcanics with dacite and tuff occurrences but did not return any anomalous 
values.

Due to the drilling success on the Sleepy Zone, Alexandria Minerals Corporation 
carried out a short drilling program west of the 2007 and 2008 drill holes in order to extend 
the mineralization westward and at depth.  Alexandria also focused on drilling near the 
copper mineralization hit by drill hole IAX-08-34 and decided to place a drill hole to the east. 

Hole IAX-09-49 was drilled 100 m west of  hole IAX-08-30 (Figure 5 and Table 
2, 3). It intersected a coarse grained magnetic gabbro (381.0 m to 396.3 m) that is 
deformed, foliated, and mineralized with 3% to 4% pyrite. At 396.3 m to 418.2 m the 
gabbro is bleached and altered with quartz and albite. The unit is cross cut with 3% 
to 4% quartz veining and mineralized with 2% to 10% pyrite.  The interval 396.3 m to 
414.70 m grades 3.01 g/t Au over 18.40 m and this includes at 396.3 m a grade of 
4.03 g/t Au over 11.90 m and also includes at 404.95 m a grade of 6.63 g/t Au over 
3.25 m (Table 3). The mineralized zone has four intersection grading over 6.00 g/t 
Au. This mineralized section in the drill hole IAX-09-49 extends the mineralized zone 
another 100 m westward, giving a strike length of 450 m, thus adding to the potential 
of the area and its resource. Drill hole IAX-09-50 positioned 140 m west of hole IAX-
09-49 tested the western most extension of the Sleepy mineralization. The drill hole 
intersected seven anomalous gold values in the first 326.6 m with grades varying 
between 0.22 g/t Au to 0.79 g/t Au and over widths up to 2.60 m. At 407.6 m a grade 
of 0.91 g/t Au over 1.75 m was intersected in sheared volcanics. From 445.7 m to 
452.6 m, the drill hole intersected the northeast trending Sleepy Lake fault.  The units 
appear to be highly sheared and faulted quartz-diorites altered with chlorite and 
silica, highly friable and mineralized with 10% to 20% pyrite.  This section assayed 
0.03 g/t Au over 9.15 m, and appears to indicate that the mineralized zone is offset.   

  On the eastern part of the Sleepy property, drill hole IAX-09-51 was located 
445 m east of drill hole IAX-08-34, and tested a deep EM anomaly.  The drill hole 
intersected 0.35 g/t Au and 0.07% Cu (Copper) over 0.7 m at 93.2 m, in a felsic to 
intermediate volcanic – dacite that is magnetic, with 2% to 3% pyrite-chalcopyrite.  At 
215.0 m there is an intersection grading 0.06 g/t Au and 0.102% Cu over 1.2 m in a 
felsic to intermediate volcanic – dacite that is magnetic and mineralized with 2% to 
3% pyrite-chalcopyrite.  At 229.1 m there is an intersection grading 0.30 g/t Au and 
0.30% Cu over 0.9 m felsic to intermediate volcanic – dacite that is magnetic and 
altered with chlorite and carbonate which is mineralized with 3% to 4% pyrite-
chalcopyrite.  The hole intersected 300.25 m of inter-layered andesitic and dacitic 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                17

volcanic rocks, weakly to moderately magnetic, of the Heva Formation.  Three 
intersections illustrated the presence or trace copper mineralization at 202.4 m to 
224.4 m a magnetic dacite altered with carbonate-chlorite and mineralized with 3% to 
4% pyrite and 1% chalcopyrite, at 224.4 m to 238.6 m a magnetic dacite with 
carbonate-chlorite alteration and mineralized with 2% to 3% pyrite and 1% to 2% 
chalcopyrite and at 299.1 m to 300.25 m an andesite-basalt with carbonate-chlorite-
epidote alteration and mineralized with 4% to 5% pyrite and 2% to 3% chalcopyrite.  
The volcanic rocks are followed at 300.25 m to 305.0 m by coarse grained massive 
crystalline gabbros.

12.0 SAMPLING METHOD AND APPROACH 

 The drill program follows a Quality Assurance/Quality Control program consistent with 
NI 43-101 and industry best practices. Drill core is NQ-sized, and is logged, sampled and 
split at the Company's Val d'Or office, in intervals of 0.3 meter to a maximum of 1.5 meters.  

13.0 SAMPLE PREPARATION, ANALYSES AND SECURITY 

 The samples are recorded, bagged and sent to Bourlamaque Assay Lab in Val-d'Or 
for assay. Samples are analyzed for Au, Ag, Cu and Zn, via a 30 grams pulp by FAA for Au 
and AA for Ag, Cu and Zn. Re-assays by FA gravimetric finish are performed on samples 
assaying greater than 1.0 g/t Au and re-assays greater than 5.0 g/t Au are checked a second 
time by FA gravimetric finish. 

14.0 DATA VERIFICATION 

 The authors confirm that the assay results listed in the previous reports and previous 
diamond drill logs are the same and a compilation of the diamond drill holes completed.  

Geologica has collected and analysed a total of 22 samples of second-half drill core 
from holes IAX-08-29 and IAX-08-30 completed by Alexandria. Geologica's samples were 
collected independently of Alexandria, kept secure and transported to the ALS Chemex 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                19

assay laboratory, Val-d'Or for fire assay using aliquots of 30 g.  For fire assay, all assays 
were finished by atomic absorption; samples that returned greater than 1 g/t Au were re-
assayed using a gravimetric finish.  Sample preparation included crushing to 70% less than 
2 mm, riffling out a 200 g fraction and pulverizing to 85% less than 75 µm.  Certificates are 
contained in Appendix IV. 

Assay results for these independent samples are listed in Table 4 and compared with 
original assays obtained by Geologica and Alexandria.   

The results confirm the presence of gold in the mineralized intervals sampled but 
correlation between original and 2nd half core sampling is generally moderate.  Geologica 
interprets this to be the result of erratically distributed relatively coarse gold in the samples 
and supports our recommendation that assays would be more representative if larger 
aliquots, say 2 assay tons or metallic screen methods were used.   

Geologica's review of Alexandria's drill core also included comparison of geology as 
reported in the drill logs with our observation made of the core.  We found that logging was to 
industry standard.  Sample descriptions were also found to be reasonably representative.  
We also checked sampled intervals in the core against those reported in the logs and found 
no discrepancies.

15.0 ADJACENT PROPERTIES 

 Ground to the north of the property is held by Beaufield Resources and Teck 
Resources comprising the Sleepy Lake South Stringer Zone, the Sleepy Lake North 
Copper Zone and the Lugold East and West mineralized zones. The northwest part of the 
property is bordered by a numbered company (6275061 Canada Inc) and hosts the old 
Sigma II Mine. South of the Sleepy property is the Trivio property, owned by Alexandria 
and is shown in Figure 6.  

16.0 MINERAL PROCESSING AND METALLURGICAL TESTING 

 In November 2009, LTM Laboratory of Val-d'Or has completed various recovery 
and metallurgical tests on seven (7) samples: one sample of 1 kg and three samples of 3 
kg, which were collected on mineralized core from DDH IAX-09-49. The samples were 
crushed at various grain sizes (400, 200, 65, 35 and 10 mesh), passed through a Knelson 
concentrator, then cyanidated and flocculated. 

 It was concluded that: the ore is easy to grind; the gold is easily recoverable by 
cyanidation; the cyanide consumption is low; gravimetric recovery with a Knelson 
concentrator does not necessarily improve recovery when the ore is concentrated prior to 
cyanidation; the best flocculent for the Sleepy property ore is Percol 338. 

 It would be advisable to continue the testing with other grinding size and cyanide 
exposition time to analyse the grinding-cyanide curves. Moreover, very fine grinding and 
concentration with a Knelson concentrator followed with longer cyanide solution 
exposition is recommended. The LTM Laboratory report is presented in Appendix VII. 

17.0 MINERAL RESOURCE AND MINERAL RESERVE ESTIMATES 

 In September 2009 Alexandria gave the mandate to Christian D'Amours of 
Geopointcom, an independent consulting firm in Val d'Or, to carry out a Resource 
estimate of the Sleepy auriferous zone. They carried out geostatistics, worked out the 
statistics parameters and selected the appropriate method of resource estimate for the 
Sleepy Lake zone.   

 The database was built up in Gemcom software. The mineralized envelopes 
(solids) were also digitized in Gems, and the mineralized envelops terminated westward 
on a northeast trending fault on Sleepy Lake.  The database validation was carried out, a 
minimum horizontal width thickness was set at 3.0 m, and a cutoff grade for the 
composites was set at 2.00 g/t Au for this model of mineralization: an altered zone 
approximating those of wide veins. These parameters are not based on economic factors 
or on a production scenario, because of the early stage of the project.



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                23

 The project has 34 drill holes of which 23 intersected the Sleepy Lake zone that is 
oriented N090 ° and dipping -83°.  The statistics demonstrates that the average width of 
the zone is 5.35 m and the intersections have an average grade of 2.33 g/t Au with six (6) 
intersections having sampling gaps, hence, assigning the grade at the gaps to 0 g/t Au.  
The statistics (Frequency % versus Length and Frequency Grades g/t Au versus Length) 
indicate that the average composite lengths of the samples selected should be set at 1.1 
m.  The frequency curves are almost log normal with a slight asymmetric tendency to the 
left.

 The cutoff grade was decided using the coefficient of variation, the probability 
curve on the superior portion, and a fractionation analysis where 10% of the superior 
metal factor expressed is less than 1% of the samples (Metal Factor). The coefficient of 
variation is 1.97 which is acceptable, and may not require cutting the high grades. The 
probability curve illustrates that most of the points are within the limits of a linear 
regression with confidence limits of 95%. The percentile of the metal factor indicates that 
16% of the total metal expressed is situated in the last percentile. To satisfy the metal 
factor, a cap grade of 33.5 g/t Au should be set. This will affect three (3) samples and 
lower the total metal by 9.5%; the average grade would be at 3.58 g/t Au instead of 3.92 
g/t Au and the Coefficient of Variation will be set at 1.57 instead of 1.97.  Due to the very 
few samples, a cutoff or cap grade of the high grades is not recommended at this stage of 
the project but will have to be reviewed when there will be more data points presented. 

 Composites closest to 1.1 m were created for each intersection, thus avoiding the 
possibility of samples being dropped at this stage. There were 192 composites created 
with average composite widths of 1.1 m (Min 0.975 m and Max 1.225 m) with an average 
grade of 3.92 g/t Au and there were 12 gap composites set at 0 g/t Au. The gap samples 
affected 10% of the composites (Table 5). 

 For the variography the authors preferred using the correlogram instead of the 
Variogram or the Semi-Variogram Standards.  The correlogram is commonly used and is 
less sensitive to erratic values.  The nugget effect counts for less than 30% of the total 
variation and the variogram axis are 1 subhorizontal (40 m), axis 2 (30 m) and the axis 

3 (8 m); an anisotropy parallel to the longitudinal axis.  (X - 268°/-04° - 40 m; Y - 163°/-
74° - 30 m; Z - 359°/-15° - 8 m). 

 The density was estimated using samples from the drill holes IAX-07-14, IAX-08-
29 and IAX-08-30 for a total of 44 samples take in ore, footwall and hanging wall.  The 
average density is 2.82 g/cm³, varying between 2.79 to 2.84 g/cm³. 

 Due to the stage of the project and average envelop widths of 5 m, it is 
recommended that cells (blocks) of 5 m x 5 m x 5 m be used, with cutoffs of 2.0 g/t Au, 
and with sub-blocks near the margins.  In Gems the origin of the blocks is at a coordinate 
of 237,126E, 5,324,789N and 3,300 (MTM); with 121 columns, 18 rows and 100 levels; a 
total of 217,800 cells (blocks). 

 Based on the correlogram, the distribution of the composites and the maturity of 
the project the authors recommend using inverse square distance anisotropy to the power 
of 2.  For the ellipse it will have to contain 2 samples without considering the origin of the 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                24

drill holes, with only the 12 samples closest to the centroid of the cell will be described as 
the search ellipsoid No.1. If it is impossible to find 2 samples within that ellipsoid then the 
3 dimensions are multiplied by 4 (Search Ellipse No.4). If no samples are found within the 
cell then the cell is not evaluated. 

 Estimates done with the search ellipse No.1 and categorized as inferred resources 
with a cutoff of 2 g/t Au. To increase to the indicated category the drill hole spacing 
intersections will have to be at 35 m X 35 m, only once the extension of the mineralization 
is found at a drill spacing of 140 m X 140 m is this recommended. 

 The estimate identified 552,163 m³ of mineralization or 1,557,000 tonnes at a 
grade of 3.00 g/t Au or 150,400 troy ounces Au of inferred category with a minimum 
horizontal thickness of 3.0 m and a cutoff grade of 2.0 g/t Au. 

 Exploration is recommended to look at extensions westward of the fault and to look 
at deeper parallel zones.

18.0 OTHER RELEVANT DATA AND INFORMATION 

 No historical environment liabilities were found to exist on the subject property. In 
terms of permitting, Alexandria required work permits for any construction of access for 
diamond drilling or stripping / trenching activities, or for clearing of lumber on the claims 
holdings.

19.0 INTERPRETATIONS AND CONCLUSION 

 The Sleepy property of Alexandria Minerals straddles the Cadillac Break, which represents 
an important metallogenic feature in the Val-d'Or area. Several past producers such as the East 
Malartic, Barnat-Sladen, and O'Brien Mines, and recent discoveries such as the Goldex and the 
Lapa projects of Agnico-Eagle Mines Inc. are in direct spatial relationship to this feature. 

 The property of Alexandria Minerals is strategically located with respect to the Cadillac 
Break and its associated conjugate auriferous structures. Several recent discoveries in the region, 
including those of Agnico Eagle and Osisko Explorations show the potential of the proximity to the 
Cadillac Break. The presence of numerous gold deposits and the exploration activities being 
conducted around them supports the idea of the potential for finding new mineralized zones 
and/or extensions of known zones on pre-existing deposits. 

Recent work on the Sleepy property has confirmed that the formerly explored and 
exploited gold bearing structures adjacent to this property continue to show potential for hosting 
additional mineralization, and merit additional exploration work. Past exploration programs in the 
area have discovered several significant gold-bearing zones on these properties, and recent 
efforts by Alexandria have shown that these past results can be built upon. Other properties of 
similar standing have been subjected to similar exploration efforts with positive results, as in the 
Malartic area, in and around the Bourlamaque Batholith, and elsewhere along the Cadillac Break. 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy Properties – Alexandria Minerals Corp.                                                25

Given the historical exploration record of the area, there is a very good possibility that 
encouraging gold results could be discovered on the Cadillac Break properties of Alexandria 
Minerals Corp.

 In addition, recent exploration activities and discoveries have shown that there is 
considerable potential below 500 meters depth, as at the Lapa discovery, reported to contain 
probable reserve of more than 1.6 M ounces of gold, mostly below 500 meters (www.agnico-
eagle.com). The prospectivity of Alexandria's land holdings is strong considering that the average 
depth of investigation by historic diamond drilling on these properties is approximately 150 
meters. The Exploration targets located at depth, along northeast oriented splays and associated 
with Z shaped folds in the host stratigraphy have historically been favorable targets especially 
along the Cadillac Break.  We also find similar situations along the Vicour Sill, a differentiated 
gabbroic sill that is deformed, foliated, penetrated by quartz veins, altered silicified and albitized 
and mineralized with pyrite and gold.  Three holes in the 2007 and 2008 drilling campaign (IAX-
08-14, IAX-08-29 and IAX-08-30) have extended the Sleepy Zone to the west and at depth 
extending the zone to a total length of 400 m east-west and 350 m depth wise vertically.  



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Report on the Cadillac Break Properties  -  Alexandria Minerals Corporation                                                                                                            26

20.0 RECOMMENDATION AND BUDGET 

Exploration on the Sleepy property will continue on the Sleepy Zone with the planning of 
fifteen (15) drill holes or 10,000 m of drilling.  The drilling will be focused principally on the western 
side of the fault extending the mineralization.  One or two holes may be placed to verify the second 
occurrence of mineralization identified in one drill hole below the main zone.

Appendix III - Sample Quality Control 

2007 Drilling and Trenching Sampling Method

For the 2007 drilling program, the core sampling protocol was established by E. 
Canova of Alexandria Minerals Corporation. Once the drilling core was extracted, the 
sampling method was as follows: 

1) Core boxes are received daily from the drilling company, opened and set on 
logging tables. 

2) The core is fitted together, washed with water and a brush, the depth markers in 
the boxes are all checked to make sure there are no depth measurement mistakes; 

3) Before logging commences, pictures of the core boxes are taken in its entirety; 
4) The core recovery and RQD of the core is then measured. 
5) Then geology and contacts are marked with a yellow wax markers and the 

descriptions are entered into an excel logging program to then be transferred into 
Gemcom.  Samples for assaying are then marked and described, the geologist 
also orients the core, marks the start and end of the sample directly onto the core 
with a red colored wax crayon while the core is still intact in the core box.  This 
would allow for the sampling of the same side of the core, the top half; 

6) The core is generally sampled over regular intervals varying between 30 cm 
minimum and 150 cm maximum; 

7) Samples are measured to the nearest centimetre, but sample intervals have to 
coincide with major lithological boundaries; 

8) A sample tag, especially made of waterproof paper and legible ink, is placed at the 
start of the sample interval.  Each sample number is unique and entered in the 
database, a distinct series is used (eg. 113835);

9) Known standards are inserted by the geologist into the core boxes; 
10) Samples are split with a hydraulic splitter and electric rock saw in a core shack in 

Val-d'Or where the core is stored.  Samples were split in half, lengthwise, using a 
hydraulic core splitter and electric rock saw in order to provide witness samples; 

11) Half the sample, top half, (assay sample) is placed separately in a plastic bag tied 
with a plastic tie rap.  The other half returns to the box according to its original 
position in the core box and retained for future reference; 

12) In the case of "grinded core", samples are taken by hand with a scoop and a 
representative part is kept in the core box; 

13) The other identical sample tag is stapled into the core box showing the sample 
number at the beginning of the marked sample interval; 

14) Each rice bag contains a maximum of 10 sample plastic bags.  The assay request 
forms specifies the name of the laboratory, the person making the request, the 
date, the sample series, assaying method, the units for the results to be reported 
(g/t Au), the analytical method and any other special instructions; 

15) One ASL (Analytical Solutions Ltd.) sample is introduced within each batch of 17 
core samples.  The ASL samples are already packaged in 60 gm sealed foiled 
bags.  The samples introduced from Ore as 15Pa with the values of gold equal to 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy property - Alexandria Minerals Corporation                               V

1.02 ppm Au (+/-0.03 ppm Au), from Ore as 54Pa with the values of gold equal to 
ppm 2.9 Au (+/-0.011 ppm Au) and the value of copper of 1.55% Cu, from Ore as 
10Pb with the value of gold equal to 7.15 ppm Au (+/-0.19 ppm Au), from Ore as 
62Pb with the values of gold equal to 11.33 ppm Au (+/-0.35ppm) and silver equal 
to 21.5 ppm Ag; 

16) Also introduced in the batch of 17 core samples is a blank sample, normally 
introduced within an area that may expect to give results.  The blank sample is 
pure silica or even diorite core with no visible sulphides from the hole AAX-07-20. 

17) Also introduced in the batch of 17 core samples is a duplicate sample of sample 
already collected for assaying, hence no core will remain for this interval. 

18) Rock samples were prepared at Bourlamaque Labs in Val-d'Or, Quebec. All 
samples underwent custom crushing and pulverizing techniques. The entire 
sample was passed through a primary crusher to yield a fine crushed product 
where greater than 95% of the sample passes through a 2mm (-10 mesh) screen. 
Samples were then riffle split to obtain approximately a one-kilogram sub-sample. 
When the crushed sample yielded approximately one kilogram the entire sample 
was pulverized.  A one-kilogram crushed sample split was ground using a ring mill 
pulverizer.  All samples were pulverized to greater than 70% of the ground material 
passing through a 75-micron screen.  Samples were analyzed at Bourlamaque 
Labs in Val-d'Or, Quebec for Au, Ag, Cu, and Zn at the Bourlamaque Labs in Val-
d'Or, Quebec. 

19) The samples are analyzed for Au by FAA – Gold Fire Assay (Pyro-SAA-020) AA 
Finish Fire Assay Fusion For fully quantitative total gold contents, the fire assay 
procedure is the preferred choice of analysis. The samples are mixed with fluxing 
agents including lead oxide, and fused at high temperature. The lead oxide is 
reduced to lead, which collects the precious metals. When the fused mixture is 
cooled, the lead remains at the bottom, while a glass-like slag remains at the top. 
The precious metals are separated from the lead in a secondary procedure called 
cupellation. The final technique used to determine the gold and other precious 
metals contents of the residue can range from a balance (for very high grade 
samples). 30-g samples were analyzed for gold using fire assay with atomic 
absorption finish (Au-AA020), giving a lower limit of detection of 5 ppb and an 
upper limit of detection of 10,000 ppb Au. For samples with > 1000 ppb Au, a 30-g 
sample was re-assayed using fire assay methods with a gravimetric finish (Au-
Pyro-SAA-010), giving a lower limit of 0.05 gpt and an upper limit of 1,000 gpt.  If 
assays surpassed 10 gpt Au then they are re-assayed by Pyro Gravimetric (Au-
Pyro-SAA-010). 

20) Samples are also analyzed for Ag (DIG-AR Ag detection 0.5 ppm), Cu (DIG-AR Cu 
detection 5ppm) and Zn (DIG-AR Zn detection 5ppm). A prepared 0.50-gram 
sample was digested with perchloric, nitric and hydrofluoric acids. The residue was 
dissolved in nitric and hydrochloric acids and diluted to a final volume with de-
ionized water. The resulting solution was analyzed by inductively coupled plasma-
atomic emission spectrometry (ICP-AES). Following this analysis, the results are 
reviewed to ensure that base metal concentrations are less than 1%, with the 
exception of silver, which have upper analytical limits of 100, 500, and 1000 ppm. 
Samples that met this criterion were then diluted and analyzed by inductively 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy property - Alexandria Minerals Corporation                               VI

coupled plasma - mass spectrometry. Results were corrected for spectral inter-
element interference. 

21) The bags are sealed with a plastic tie rap, a lab requisition form is filled up with the 
instructions for the assay procedure, samples to be assayed and form of assay 
result presentation.  The samples are then brought by the P.Geo geologist to the 
lab and the requisition form is signed for reception of the samples by a person from 
the lab; 

22) Internal Bourlamaque Lab Quality Control Procedures – Bourlamaque Lab 
standard operating procedures require the analysis of quality control samples 
(reference materials, duplicates and blanks) with all sample batches. As part of the 
assessment of every data set, results from the control samples are evaluated to 
ensure they meet set standards determined by the precision and accuracy 
requirements of the method. 

In the event that any reference material or duplicate result falls outside the 
established control limits, an Error Report is automatically generated. This ensures 
the person evaluating the sample set for data release is made aware that a 
problem may exist with the data set and investigation can be initiated. 

All data generated from quality control samples is automatically captured and 
retained in a separate database used for Quality Assessment.  Control charts for 
in-house reference materials from frequently used analytical methods are regularly 
generated and evaluated by senior technical staff at Quality Assurance meetings to 
ensure internal specifications for precision and accuracy are being met. Quality 
control data for reference materials and duplicates are routinely reported to clients 
so that they may monitor laboratory data independently. These reports are 
generated at no charge to the client and are issued together with the Certificates of 
Analysis. 

23) Each rice bag contains 10 samples tied with a plastic tie rap to seal the bags, and 
these are then brought to the laboratory. 



Geologica Groupe – Conseil Inc.

NI 43-101 Technical Report on the Sleepy property - Alexandria Minerals Corporation                               VII

1

Introduction et mandat 

En septembre 2009, monsieur Eddy Canova confiait à Géopointcom le mandat d'estimer les 
ressources pour le projet Sleepy situé dans le secteur de Val-d'Or. Monsieur Canova agissait ainsi 
au nom d'Alexandria Minérals Corporation (« Le client »).  Le présent mandat consiste à 
sélectionner les paramètres géostatistiques appropriés pour l'estimation des ressources et à faire 
toutes les observations et recommandations pertinentes pour le développement du potentiel 
économique de ce projet.  

L'auteur n'a pas visité le terrain visé et n'a pas fait une vérification poussée des données soumises 
par le client puisque ces étapes seront réalisées par un autre consultant qui aura le mandat de 
réaliser une étude conforme à la norme 43-101. La présente étude couvrira essentiellement la 
section 19 (Estimation des ressources minérales et des réserves minérales) prévue à la norme 43-
101 et pourra donc être incluse ou référencée dans un autre rapport, plus complet, qui lui, sera 
conforme à la règlementation en vigueur.  

À la demande du client, toutes les données transmises par celui-ci pour la réalisation de ce 
mandat sont considérées comme confidentielles et devront être traitées comme telle à la fin 
du mandat.   

Données sources. 

La documentation source est constituée d'une base de données au format Gemcom contenant les 
forages ainsi que les models filaires de la zone Sleepy et d'une faille marquant la limite Ouest de la 
zone minéralisée. (Voir fichiers sources sur le DVD en annexe) 

La base de données couvre un secteur beaucoup plus étendu que le projet sous étude. Aussi 
l'auteur a limité la sélection des forages à un secteur proximal à la zone Sleepy. 

Sélection des échantillons et statistiques. 

La sélection d'échantillons présents dans les limites du modèle filaire fourni par le client présentait 
des intersections larges à très basse teneur. Après avoir corrigé quelques erreurs dans la table de 
déviation des forages, l'auteur a revu toutes les intersections en considérant une épaisseur minimale 
de 3 mètres horizontal et un « cutoff » de 2g/t. Le modèle filaire a aussi été revu afin de respecter la 
nouvelle sélection.  

L'épaisseur minimale ainsi que le « cutoff » utilisés dans cette étude, ne sont pas appuyés sur une 
évaluation économique ou une planification d'exploitation détaillée du projet qui permettrait 
éventuellement un investissement majeur de capitaux. Vue le caractère juvénile du secteur sous 
étude, l'auteur a plutôt utilisé des paramètres (épaisseur minimale, cutoff) généraux situés 
légèrement du côté optimiste permettant  aux lecteurs avisés de se faire une bonne idée du potentiel 
économique du projet et ainsi prendre les bonnes décisions (plus éclairées) concernant les suivis à 
donner à ce projet d'exploration. 

La liste des intersections considérées est présentée au tableau 1.  Sur les 34 forages considérés, 23 
ont intersectés la zone Sleepy. Les 11 autres forages sont soit trop courts, soit mal positionnés  ou 



2

soit de l'autre coté de la faille mais n'ont pas intersectés la cible. Les 23 forages positifs définissent 
donc un plan assez rectiligne orienté N090 avec un pendage vers le sud de -83º.  

Le plan ainsi défini,  a une épaisseur horizontale moyenne de 5.35m et les intersections ont une 
teneur moyenne de 2.33 g/t Au.

IAX-08-30 Sleepy 350.70 357.25 3.12 3.85
IAX-09-49 Sleepy 396.30 408.19 8.27 3.85

Il est important de souligner que six (6) intersections (voir tableau 1A) contiennent des portions non 
échantillonnées (gap). Pour les besoins de cette étude, ces portions ont été fixées à 0g/t. Cependant 
puisqu'au moins quatre (4) de ces intersections sont localisées à des points stratégiques (voir 
projection longitudinale en annexe) et que ces « gaps » représentent des longueurs non 
négligeables (2.48m en moyenne), l'auteur recommande fortement qu'un effort particulier soit 
apporté affin de corriger la situation, spécialement pour le trou BS88-20.  



3

devrait pas avoir d'effet sur la teneur moyenne simplement un léger effet de lissage tel que présenté 
au tableau 3.

4

L'observation des informations présentées au tableau 4 montrent clairement une distribution 
légèrement asymétrique (côté gauche), presque log-normale de Au. Cette distribution n'est pas très 
courante pour une distribution aurifère. Généralement, l'asymétrie se situe plutôt du côté droit. 
L'auteur est d'avis que cette observation est principalement due au peu d'information disponible et 
que l'augmentation de la quantité d'information conduira à une courbe différente.  La courbe de 
probabilité est assez loin d'une droite mais dans le secteur des hautes valeurs, les points restent bien 
en deçà des limites d'un intervalle de confiance de 95%. Finalement, l'observation du fractionnement 
en percentile montre que 16% du métal se retrouve dans le dernier percentile.  

Coupure des hautes valeurs (Capping). 

Pour établir la limite de coupure pour les hautes valeurs, l'auteur utilise trois critères distincts. Le 
coefficient de variation CV doit être le plus bas possible, idéalement inférieur à 2. La courbe de 
probabilité, surtout la portion supérieure,  doit être le plus près possible d'une droite sans présenter 
de changement de pente positif important. Finalement l'analyse de fractionnement en percentile ne 
doit pas révéler plus de 10% du métal exprimé dans moins de 1% des échantillons (facteur métal). 

Le coefficient de variation (tableau 4) est de 1.97 ce qui est une limite acceptable laissant présumer 
qu'il ne serait peut être pas nécessaire de couper les hautes valeurs. Tel qu'il a été dit 
précédemment, bien que la portion supérieure de la courbe de probabilité présente un changement 
de pente évident, tous les points restent bien à l'intérieur des limites d'une régression linéaire avec 
un  intervalle de confiance de 95%. Finalement, l'examen du fractionnement  percentile  montre que 
16% du métal total exprimé se situe dans le dernier percentile. Pour satisfaire à la règle du facteur 
métal, on devrait limiter les hautes valeurs aurifères à 33.5 g/t (ligne verte sur le graphique de 
probabilité). Cette coupure affecterait 3 échantillons et réduirait de 9.5% le métal total exprimé. La 
moyenne simple passerait de 3.92 à 3.58 et le CV passerait à 1.57.   

En considérant le caractère juvénile du projet (très peu d'échantillons) et que seule la règle 
du facteur métal prône en faveur d'une limitation des hautes valeurs, l'auteur propose de ne 
pas appliquer de teneur de coupure pour les hautes valeurs aurifères.  Cette 
recommandation devrait être revue suite à l'ajout de nouvelles intersections. Si la teneur de 
couture suggérée par la règle du facteur métal venait à se confirmer, il sera alors bien avisé 
de l'appliquer.

Création des composites. 

La méthode utilisée par l'auteur consiste à créer des composites égaux le plus près possible de 1.1 
pour chaque intersection. Cette méthode présente l'avantage de ne pas laisser tomber des portions 
d'échantillons à la fin de chaque intersection.  Par contre les composites ne seront pas tous 
exactement de la même longueur.   

L'auteur a donc créé 192 composites d'une longueur moyenne de 1.1m (minimum 0.975 ; maximum 
1.225) ayant une teneur aurifère moyenne de 3.92 g/t. Notez que les secteurs non échantillonnés (gap) 
discutés plus haut, ont contribué à créer 12 composites d'une valeur 0 g/t et à diminuer la teneur de 4 
ou 5 autres composites. Ces « gaps » ont donc affectés près de 10% des composites utilisés pour 
l'estimation des ressources. 

Le tableau 5 présente plusieurs graphiques qui démontrent clairement que l'étape de création des 
composites ne produit pas de biais notable  sur la distribution des teneurs. 

Tableau 5 : Composites Vs échantillons coupé. 



7

Variographie. 

L'auteur a modélisé la variographie des composites de la zone Sleepy en utilisant le logiciel « Sage 
2001 ».  L'auteur a préféré utiliser la méthode de corrélogramme plutôt que des variogrammes ou 
des semi-variogrammes standards. Cette méthode est largement utilisée dans l'industrie et présente 
l'avantage d'être moins sensible aux valeurs erratiques et surtout aux mailles irrégulières (clustering). 
Les buts de cette étape consiste à : 

- Caractériser l'anisotropie et ainsi fixer les dimensions et l'orientation d'un ellipsoïde de recherche 
à utiliser lors de l'interpolation des teneurs du modèle de bloc. Les dimensions des trois axes de 
l'ellipsoïde seront égales aux portées  mesurées sur les variogrammes. De cette façon il est 
démontré statistiquement que peu importe où est situé le centre de cet ellipsoïde, tous les 
échantillons inclus à l'intérieur de celui-ci auront une variance inférieur à celle de la population 
entière.  Il est alors raisonnable d'utiliser cette sous-sélection pour estimer la valeur du point 
central. L'anisotropie peut aussi être utilisée pour sélectionner et pondérer les échantillons lors 
des étapes de « de-clustering ». 

- Aider à la classification des ressources. La géométrie de l'ellipsoïde de recherche est souvent 
utilisée pour classifier les différentes catégories de ressources. Si suffisamment d'échantillons se 
trouvent à l'intérieur des limites de l'ellipsoïde, on considère généralement être en mesure 
d'estimer, avec un degré de confiance acceptable, la valeur au point central de ce volume.  

- Définir les équations de Krigeage. Les équations dérivées des variogrammes sont nécessaires 
lors d'une interpolation par Krigeage. Ces équations prennent en compte l'effet pepitique (C0), le 
modèle de dispersion (sphérique, exponentiel…), la portée et la variance dans chacun des 3 
axes ( 1, 2 et 3). Il est fréquent d'utiliser plus de un modèle afin de mieux représenter la 
dispersion de chacun des axes avant d'atteindre le palier (variance totale). 

L'auteur a d'abord calculé un corrélogramme omnidirectionnel (contrôlé par les forages) pour estimer 
l'effet pépitique (C0).  Dans un deuxième temps, il a calculé 73 corrélogrammes directionnels 
(espacés de 30º horizontal et de 15º vertical) disposés de façon à couvrir également toutes les 
directions disponibles sur une sphère. Pour chacun de ces corrélogrammes, l'auteur a utilisé un lag 
de 5m et limité la sélection à un rectangle de 20m X 20m ainsi qu'un angle de tolérance de 10º le 
long de chacun des axes.  

Cette étape permet d'avoir une vue d'ensemble de la variance sur une sphère idéalisée. L'auteur 
utilise ensuite un utilitaire de calcul de régression (inclus dans le logiciel Sage 2001) pour trouver 
l'orientation des portées les plus longues. Puisque le résultat obtenu correspond très bien à une 
solution possible située sur le plan idéalisé de la zone, l'auteur n'a pas forcé de solution coplanaire 
au plan idéalisé. Finalement, il ne reste plus qu'à calculer les corrélogrammes selon les trois 
meilleures directions. Ce sont ces corrélogrammes qui sont présentés ici. Notez que pour la direction  

3 le lag a été réduit à 1 mètre avec un angle de tolérance de 45º. 

Les corrélogrammes obtenus sont considérés robustes et fiables. C'est-à-dire qu'ils résistent assez 
bien à des changements de paramètres tels que la tolérance ou le lag et qu'ils se comparent bien 
avec les résultats obtenus en utilisant les variogrammes standard ou les semi-variogrammes. Les 
tableaux 6 et 7 présentent les résultats obtenus ainsi que les différents réglages permettant d'obtenir 
ces rotations en utilisant le logiciel Gemcom. 



8

Selon le tableau 6, l'effet pépitique compte pour un peu moins de 30% de la variation totale. L'axe 1
est sub-horizontale et pratiquement de la même portée que l'axe 2 (40 et 30 mètres). L'axe 3 est 5 
fois plus court (8 mètres). Il s'agit donc d'une anisométrie modérée pratiquement parallèle au plan 
idéalisé de la longitudinale.  L'auteur a emboîté deux modèles sphériques de dimensions 
comparables permettant ainsi de bien caractériser la corrélation des pairs en fonction de la distance. 

Les axes 2 et 3 sont particulièrement bien documentés, par contre, l'axe 1 souffre un peu du 
manque de pairs.

Densité du minerai. 

Pour estimer la densité du minerai, l'auteur a eu accès à 44 mesures de la gravité spécifique.  Ces 
mesures ont été prises à partir de 3 forages (IAX-07-14, IAX-08-29 et IAX-08-30). Les analyses 
proviennent en part égales du minerai, de l'éponte inférieure et de l'éponte supérieure. Le client a 
d'abord suggéré de n'utiliser que les échantillons provenant du minerai. De par la nature du minerai, 
l'auteur a vérifié, à l'aide des équations de Student, s'il existait une différence entre les mesures 
provenant du minerai, de l'éponte inférieure et de l'éponte supérieure. Sans grande surprise, il est 
démontré qu'il n'y a pas de différences significatives entre ces trois sources. Pour continuer le 
raisonnement, l'auteur a vérifié s'il existait des différences entre les trois forages en considérant 
indifféremment la provenance (minerai ou épontes). Les équations de Student permettent alors de 
dire que les analyses de SG provenant du trou IAX-07-14 sont statistiquement supérieures à celles 
provenant du IAX-08-29 et que les analyses du trou IAX-08-29 sont statistiquement plus élevées que 
celle du trou IAX-08-30. 

Pour le moment et faute de mieux, la moyenne simple des 44 analyses est considérée la meilleure 
estimation du SG de la zone Sleepy.  Selon l'auteur, la meilleure estimation de SG est 2.82  g/cm3. À 
95% de confiance elle variera entre 2.79 et 2.84 g/cm3.  



10

Géométrie du modèle de bloc. 

Compte tenu de la géométrie des enveloppes minéralisées (sub-vertical avec 5 mètres de largeur) et 
qu'il s'agit d'une estimation préliminaire sans besoin d'optimisation des épontes ( pas de planification 
de minage associé) l'auteur recommande d'utiliser des cellules de 5X5X5. Ce modèle de blocs 
facilitera le travail lors de la sélection de l'enveloppe finale (cutoff = 2 g/t).   

L'auteur ne recommande pas d'utiliser des sous-blocs mais plutôt de créer des blocs de type 
« partiel » permettant d'évaluer le pourcentage de chaque unité  présente dans chaque cellule. 

Selon la notation Gemcom, l'origine du bloc est localisée à la coordonnée  [237126 ; 5324789 ; 
3300]. Le modèle comprend 121 colonnes, 18 rangés et 100 niveaux, soit une possibilité de 217 800 
cellules. 

Méthode et paramètres d'estimation. 

En se basant sur les corrélogrammes obtenus (tableau 6), la distribution des composites et le degré 
de maturité du projet, l'auteur suggère d'interpoler la teneur des cellules en utilisant l'inverse de la 
distance anisotropique élevée à la puissance 2 (IPD2).  Les échantillons à utiliser pour l'interpolation 
des cellules seront sélectionnés en utilisant un ellipsoïde de recherche identique à celui proposé au 
tableau 7.  

Pour qu'un ellipsoïde soit considéré emplis, il devra contenir au moins 2 échantillons sans égard au 
forage d'origine ni aux octants de sélection. Seuls les 12 échantillons les plus près du centre seront 
utilisés. Cet ellipsoïde est décrit comme l'ellipsoïde de recherche numéro 1. S'il est impossible de 
trouver au moins 2 échantillons à l'intérieur des limites de l'ellipsoïde numéro 1, les trois dimensions 
sont alors multipliés par 4 et les mêmes paramètres de minimum et maximum sont appliqués. Il s'agit 
alors de l'ellipsoïde de recherche numéro 4. S'il est toujours impossible de trouver au moins 2 
échantillons alors la cellule reste non évaluée. 

Finalement, la sélection de l'enveloppe « économique » se fait en traçant le contour, en longitudinale, 
des cellules contigües estimées à 2.00 g/t et plus (Voir Projection longitudinale.pdf en annexe). 

À un stade aussi précoce du développement d'une zone minéralisée, l'auteur considère inutile 
d'investir temps et argent à des étapes de validation et d'optimisation des procédures d'estimation de 
ressources. 



11

Estimation des ressources. 

Il est d'usage courant dans l'industrie d'utiliser la limite de l'ellipsoïde de recherche numéro 1 pour 
séparer les ressources inférées des ressources indiquées. Évidemment, pour que cette approche 
soit significative, la géométrie de l'ellipsoïde de recherche doit être basée sur les portées d'une 
variographie adéquate. Par définition, si l'ellipsoïde est bien construit, la variance des échantillons 
sélectionnés sera inférieure à celle des échantillons plus éloignés. L'utilisation de l'ellipsoïdes est 
donc un bon outil pour identifier les cellules ou la confiance en la teneur estimée est plus grande 
(variance plus faible). Cependant, la confiance en la teneur n'est pas le seul facteur à considérer lors 
de la classification des ressources. Il faut aussi tenir compte de la confiance (continuité) géologique. 
Dans certain cas, une maille de forage plus serrée est nécessaire pour permettre une modélisation 
fiable et précise de la minéralisation.  

Dans le cas qui nous intéresse, les cellules interpolées avec l'ellipsoïde numéro 1 forment des îlots 
isolés et représentent seulement 30 % des cellules incluses dans l'enveloppe « cutoff » à 2.00 g/t. 
L'auteur considère donc toutes les cellules, incluant celles estimées avec l'ellipsoïde numéro1, 
comme appartenant à la catégorie ressources inférées. 

Pour augmenter la confiance et permettre d'atteindre la catégorie « indiquées », la maille de forage 
devra idéalement s'approcher de 35X35. 

La présente estimation a permis d'identifier un volume de 552 163 m3 de minerai soit 1 557 000 
tonnes métriques titrant 3.00 g/t (150 400 onces troy) à placer dans la catégorie « Ressources 
inférées ». 



12

Conclusions et recommandations. 

En considérant une épaisseur horizontale minimale de 3m et un « cutoff » de 2.00 g/t, les ressources 
inférées de la zone Sleepy sont estimées à 1 557 000 t de minerais titrant 3.00 g/t soit un total de 
150 400 onces. 

Selon le client, l'extension de cette zone doit être recherché à l'Ouest de la faille bordant la limite 
Ouest de la zone (voir plan et longitudinale en annexe). Si cette hypothèse s'avérait exacte,  avant 
de planifier une campagne d'exploration de l'autre coté de la faille, l'auteur considère qu'il serait  
important de vérifier la possibilité d'un doublage de la zone particulièrement entre les sections 
237150E et  237350E mais aussi beaucoup plus à l'Est(Voir plan et sections en annexe). Toujours 
selon cette hypothèse, il serait important de considérer que les trous IAX-08-35 et BS-05-30 ont 
sondé une partie de ce secteur. De la même façon, les trous IAX-09-50 et IAX-09-49 devraient être 
approfondis. 

L'auteur, recommande aussi de ne pas négliger la possibilité d'une extension en profondeur 
directement sous les forages IAX-09-49, IAX-08-30 et IAX-08-28. 

Cette étude a aussi fait ressortir la présence de plusieurs intervalles non analysés localisés à 
l'intérieur des limites minéralisées. L'auteur considère primordiale de remédier à cette situation. Une 
ré-analyse de ces secteurs pourrait, entre autres, changer énormément les données du trou BS-88-
20. 

Pour amener les ressources à la catégorie de « Ressources indiquées », il serait nécessaire de 
prévoir une maille de forage d'environ 35X35 mais l'auteur ne favorise pas ce type de campagne 
avant d'avoir trouvé l'extension de la zone.  La recherche de l'extension pourrait se faire en utilisant 
une maille de 140X140. Ce type de maille présente l'avantage d'être facilement transformable en 
35X35 dans le cas où l'extension serait trouvé.  



13
